The Inherence Proof for Eternal Speech
Razi presents the inherence dilemma as a proof for the eternity of God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof for the eternity of God's speech, which is based on the impossibility of speech inhering in God or being separate from Him.

Core Idea
If God's speech were temporal, it would either inhere in God or not, both impossible.

Razi presents a second dialectical proof: if God's speech were temporal, it would have to come to be either in God's essence or outside it. Both options are impossible—inherence would make God a locus of temporal events, and non-inherence would mean the attribute is not present in God, contradicting the fact that speech is an attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Read the Arabic passage from 'الثاني : وهو أن هذا الكلام...' to '...وذلك محال'. Understand the two-horned dilemma.
2
Analyze the two options
The proof considers two possibilities: (1) speech inheres in God's essence, making Him a locus of temporal events, which is impossible. (2) Speech does not inhere in God, which is impossible because an attribute must be in its subject.
The argument assumes that temporal events cannot inhere in God.
3
Understand the analogy
Razi adds that if an attribute could exist without inhering in its subject, then a body could be moving by a movement in another body, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : كلام الله تعالى قديم خلافا للمعتزلة والكرامية

واعلم أن الجمهور منا يعتقدون أن المعتزلة يوافقوننا في كونه تعالى متكلما ويخالفوننا في قدم الكلام ، فأما نحن قد بينا أن الذي يقول به المعتزلة فنحن نقول به من حيث المعنى والذي نقول به فهم لا يقولون به البتة، فإذا حاولنا مكالمة المعتزلة وجب علينا أن نحقق ماهية الكلام ثم نقيم الدلالة على أن الله تعالى موصوف بها ثم نقيم الدلالة على قدمها فإنهم يخالفوننا في المواضع الثلاثة فنقول .

أما المقامان الأولان وهما المقامان الصعبان مع المعتزلة فقد تقدم القول فيهما

وأما الثالث فالدليل عليه من وجهين .

الأول : أن الفريقان قائلان قائل اعترف بكون الله تعالى موصوفا بهذا الكلام وقائل أنكر ذلك ، وكل من اعترف به قال إنه قديم، لأن المعتزلة والكرامية لم يعترفوا بكون الله تعالى موصوفا بهذا الكلام وإنما قالوا بحدوث الكلام الذي يكون حرفا وصوتا ، وإذا ثبت ذلك فلو قلنا بحدوث هذا الكلام كان ذلك قولا ثالثا وهو خرق الإجماع وهو باطل .

الثاني : وهو أن هذا الكلام لو كان محدثا لكان إما أن يحدث في ذات الله تعالى فيكون محلا للحوادث وهو محال أو لا يحدث فيه وهو محال ، لأن كون الله تعالى متكلما قد دللنا على أنه من صفاته وصفة الشيء يستحيل أن لا تكون حاصلة فيه وإلا لجاز أن يكون الجسم متحركا بحركة قائمة بالغير وذلك محال واحتجوا بأمور . أولها : أن الأمر بلا مأمور عبث وهو غير جائز على الله تعالى .

وثانيها : أنه تعالى في الأزل لو كان متكلما بقوله إنا أرسلنا نوحا وهو إخبار عن الماضي لكان كاذبا

وثالثها : أن الأمة مجمعة على أن كلام الله ناسخ ومنسوخ وسور وآيات وذلك من صفات المحدثات .

والجواب عن الأول : أن عبد الله بن سعيد ذهب إلى أن كلام الله تعالى وإن كان قديما لكنه ما كان في الأزل أمرا ولا نهيا ولا خبرا ثم صار فيما لا يزال كذلك وهذا في غاية البعد، لأنا لما وجدنا في النفس طلبا واقتضاء وبينا الفرق بينه وبين الإرادة أمكننا بعد ذلك أن نشير إلى ماهية معقولة وندعي ثبوتها لله تعالى فأما الكلام الذي يغاير هذه الحروف والأصوات ويغاير ماهية الأمر والنهي والخبر فغير معلوم التصور فإن القول بثبوته لله تعالى في الأزل محض الجهالة

أما جمهور الأصحاب : فقد زعموا أن كلام الله تعالى كان أمرا ونهيا في الأزل ، ثم منهم من يقول المعدوم مأمور على تقدير الوجود وهذا في غاية البعد ، لأن الجماد إذا لم يجز أن يكون مأمورا فالمعدوم أولى ، والذي هو في محض العدم كيف يعقل أن يكون مأمورا ومنهم من قال إنه في الأزل كان أمرا من غير مأمور، ثم لما استمر وبقي صار المكلفون بعد دخولهم في الوجود مأمورين بذلك الأمر وضربوا له مثالا وهو أن الإنسان إذا أخبره النبي الصادق بأن الله تعالى سيرزقه ولدا ولكنه مات قبل ولادته فإنه ربما قال لبعض الناس إذا أدركت ولدي بالغا فقل له أباك يأمرك بتحصيل العلم فهنا قد وجد الأمر والمأمور معدوم ، حتى أنه لو بقي ذلك الأمر إلى أوان بلوغ ذلك الصبي لصار مأمورا بذلك الأمر .
Question: The speech of God, exalted, is eternal, contrary to the Mu'tazila and Karramiyya.

Know that the majority of us believe that the Mu'tazila agree with us that He, exalted, is speaking but disagree with us on the eternity of speech. As for us, we have shown that what the Mu'tazila affirm, we affirm it with respect to meaning, and what we affirm, they do not affirm at all. So if we attempt to debate the Mu'tazila, we must verify the essence of speech, then establish the proof that God, exalted, is described by it, then establish the proof of its eternity, for they disagree with us in the three points. We say:

As for the first two points, which are the two difficult points with the Mu'tazila, the discussion has already preceded on them.

As for the third, the proof for it is from two aspects:

First: that the parties are two: one who affirms that God, exalted, is described by this speech, and one who denies that. And everyone who affirmed it said it is eternal, because the Mu'tazila and Karramiyya did not affirm that God, exalted, is described by this speech, but only said that the speech which is composed of letters and sounds is temporal. And if that is established, then if we said this speech is temporal, that would be a third opinion, which breaks consensus, and that is false.

Second: that this speech, if it were temporal, then either it would come to be in the essence of God, exalted, so He would be a locus for temporal events, which is impossible, or it would not come to be in Him, which is impossible, because that God, exalted, is speaking we have already proved that it is one of His attributes, and it is impossible for a thing's attribute not to be present in it, otherwise it would be permissible for a body to be moving by a movement subsisting in another, and that is impossible. And they argue with things: First: that a command without a commanded person is absurd, and that is not permissible for God, exalted. Second: that He, exalted, in pre-eternity, if He were speaking by His saying 'Indeed, We sent Noah,' which is an informing about the past, He would be lying. Third: that the community is agreed that the speech of God is abrogating and abrogated, and surahs and verses, and that is among the characteristics of temporal things.

The answer to the first: that Abdullah bin Saeed went to the view that the speech of God, exalted, though eternal, was not in pre-eternity a command nor a prohibition nor a report, then it became so in what will be, and this is extremely far-fetched, because when we find in the soul a demand and requirement and we have shown the difference between it and will, we can then point to an intelligible essence and claim its existence for God, exalted. As for the speech that differs from these letters and sounds and differs from the essence of command, prohibition, and report, its conception is unknown, and the statement asserting its existence for God, exalted, in pre-eternity is pure ignorance.

As for the majority of the companions: they held that the speech of God, exalted, was command and prohibition in pre-eternity. Then among them are those who say that the non-existent is commanded on the assumption of existence, and this is extremely far-fetched, because if an inanimate object cannot be commanded, then the non-existent is even more so. How can it be understood that what is in pure non-existence be commanded? And among them are those who say that it was in pre-eternity a command without a commanded person, then when it continued and remained, the obligated persons after their coming into existence become commanded by that command. And they gave an example for this: when a truthful prophet informs a man that God, exalted, will give him a son, but he dies before his birth, he might say to some people: 'If you catch my son as an adult, tell him: Your father commands you to acquire knowledge.' So here the command exists while the commanded person is non-existent, until if that command remains until the time of that boy's reaching adulthood, he would become commanded by that command.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive question (mas'ala) on the eternity of God's speech (kalam). The author begins by noting the agreement on God being speaking (mutakallim) but disagreement on temporality. He identifies three points of dispute: the essence of speech, the ascription to God, and its eternity. The first two were covered earlier. For the third, he gives two proofs. The first proof is by consensus: all who affirm that God is described by this speech say it is eternal; to say it is temporal would break consensus. The second proof: if speech were temporal, it would either inhere in God (making Him a locus of events) or not inhere (impossible for an attribute). He then presents three Mu'tazilite objections: (1) command without a commanded person is absurd, (2) if eternal speech included past-tense reports, it would be false, (3) the Quran's abrogation and verses indicate temporality. The author answers the first objection by discussing Abdullah bin Saeed's view (speech was not command/prohibition/report in pre-eternity) but finds it unsatisfactory. Then he presents the Ash'ari view: speech is eternal and includes commands and prohibitions even with non-existent commanded persons, using the example of a man commanding his future son through a proxy.

Key Terms
محدث
محل
حوادث
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's speech could be temporal without affecting His immutability.
Correction: Razi argues that temporal speech would require inherence, which God is free from, or external existence, which contradicts speech being an attribute of God.

Checkpoint
What does Razi identify as the consequence if God's speech were temporal and did not inhere in God?
A) It would be impermissible for God to be speaking.
B) The attribute would not be present in its subject, which is impossible.
C) God would be lying.
D) The speech would have to be composed of letters.

Key Takeaway
The inherence dilemma shows that God's speech cannot be temporal because it would force an impossible scenario.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that the Qur'an is the eternal, uncreated speech of God, how would your daily engagement with it change? Would you approach it with more awe, more urgency? What one concrete change can you make starting today?
?
Razi's proof shows that if God's speech were temporal, He would either be changeable or His attribute would be detached from Him. Do you ever act as if God's attributes are changeable—for example, by assuming His mercy or anger depends on your actions in a way that contradicts His eternal nature? How can you realign your view with this proof?
?
The analogy of a body moving by a movement in another highlights the absurdity of attributes existing apart from their subject. In what areas of your faith do you tend to separate God's attributes from His essence? What step can you take this week to affirm the unity and eternity of His attributes in your worship?

Responding to Three Mu'tazilite Objections
Razi enumerates three Mu'tazilite objections and provides the Ash'ari response, focusing on the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three common objections against eternal speech and the Ash'ari responses, including the solution to the problem of command without a commanded person.

Core Idea
Objections about absurdity, falsehood, and temporality of the Quran are refuted by affirming the eternal nature of divine attributes.

After presenting proofs, Razi addresses three Mu'tazilite objections: (1) eternal command without a commanded person is absurd, (2) eternal reports about future events would be false, (3) the Quran's abrogation and verses indicate temporality. He then discusses the response, focusing on the first objection and presenting the Ash'ari view that eternal commands exist and apply when commanded persons come into existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Read the three objections carefully. Note how each one challenges the concept of eternal speech.
The objections are: command without commanded, false past-tense reports, and abrogation indicating temporality.
2
Understand the response to the first objection
Razi first discusses Abdullah bin Saeed's view that speech was not command/prohibition/report in pre-eternity, but finds it unsatisfactory. Then he presents the Ash'ari view that commands and prohibitions are eternal and address non-existent persons on the assumption of existence.
He gives an analogy of a living man commanding his future son through a proxy.
3
Recognize the key argument
The Ash'ari solution is that the command itself is eternal, and it awaits the existence of the commanded person to become applicable.
This preserves the eternality of speech while addressing the objection.

مسألة : كلام الله تعالى قديم خلافا للمعتزلة والكرامية

واعلم أن الجمهور منا يعتقدون أن المعتزلة يوافقوننا في كونه تعالى متكلما ويخالفوننا في قدم الكلام ، فأما نحن قد بينا أن الذي يقول به المعتزلة فنحن نقول به من حيث المعنى والذي نقول به فهم لا يقولون به البتة، فإذا حاولنا مكالمة المعتزلة وجب علينا أن نحقق ماهية الكلام ثم نقيم الدلالة على أن الله تعالى موصوف بها ثم نقيم الدلالة على قدمها فإنهم يخالفوننا في المواضع الثلاثة فنقول .

أما المقامان الأولان وهما المقامان الصعبان مع المعتزلة فقد تقدم القول فيهما

وأما الثالث فالدليل عليه من وجهين .

الأول : أن الفريقان قائلان قائل اعترف بكون الله تعالى موصوفا بهذا الكلام وقائل أنكر ذلك ، وكل من اعترف به قال إنه قديم، لأن المعتزلة والكرامية لم يعترفوا بكون الله تعالى موصوفا بهذا الكلام وإنما قالوا بحدوث الكلام الذي يكون حرفا وصوتا ، وإذا ثبت ذلك فلو قلنا بحدوث هذا الكلام كان ذلك قولا ثالثا وهو خرق الإجماع وهو باطل .

الثاني : وهو أن هذا الكلام لو كان محدثا لكان إما أن يحدث في ذات الله تعالى فيكون محلا للحوادث وهو محال أو لا يحدث فيه وهو محال ، لأن كون الله تعالى متكلما قد دللنا على أنه من صفاته وصفة الشيء يستحيل أن لا تكون حاصلة فيه وإلا لجاز أن يكون الجسم متحركا بحركة قائمة بالغير وذلك محال واحتجوا بأمور . أولها : أن الأمر بلا مأمور عبث وهو غير جائز على الله تعالى .

وثالثها : أن الأمة مجمعة على أن كلام الله ناسخ ومنسوخ وسور وآيات وذلك من صفات المحدثات .

والجواب عن الأول : أن عبد الله بن سعيد ذهب إلى أن كلام الله تعالى وإن كان قديما لكنه ما كان في الأزل أمرا ولا نهيا ولا خبرا ثم صار فيما لا يزال كذلك وهذا في غاية البعد، لأنا لما وجدنا في النفس طلبا واقتضاء وبينا الفرق بينه وبين الإرادة أمكننا بعد ذلك أن نشير إلى ماهية معقولة وندعي ثبوتها لله تعالى فأما الكلام الذي يغاير هذه الحروف والأصوات ويغاير ماهية الأمر والنهي والخبر فغير معلوم التصور فإن القول بثبوته لله تعالى في الأزل محض الجهالة

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive question (mas'ala) on the eternity of God's speech (kalam). The author begins by noting the agreement on God being speaking (mutakallim) but disagreement on temporality. He identifies three points of dispute: the essence of speech, the ascription to God, and its eternity. The first two were covered earlier. For the third, he gives two proofs. Then he presents the Ash'ari view: speech is eternal and includes commands and prohibitions even with non-existent commanded persons, using the example of a man commanding his future son through a proxy.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that an eternal command cannot be valid if there is no one to command at that moment.

Checkpoint
How does the majority of Ash'ari scholars (جمهور الأصحاب) respond to the objection that an eternal command without a commanded person is absurd?
A) They deny that God's speech is eternal.
B) They say the command is eternal and applies when the commanded person exists, like a proxy command.
C) They claim the non-existent is actually commanded.
D) They say the command is created at the time of the commanded person.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position resolves the objection of command without commanded by affirming the eternal nature of the command and its applicability upon the existence of the commanded person.

Divine Attributes

The Eternality of Allah's Speech: Statement and Two Proofs
Razi states the Ash'ari position and gives two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the eternality of divine speech and the two proofs Razi offers to support it, as well as the key disagreement with the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya.

Core Idea
Divine speech is eternal; the Mu'tazila deny the very attribute, not just its eternality.

Razi opens this issue by clarifying that the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya do not merely disagree about the eternality of speech—they deny the very attribute of speech that the Ash'aris affirm. After outlining the correct method for debating, he presents two decisive proofs: one from consensus and one from the impossibility of accidents in Allah's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the three-step method Razi proposes.
2
Identify the three positions
Razi contrasts the Ash'ari view with the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya. Understand what each group affirms and denies.
The Mu'tazila affirm a temporal speech of letters and sounds, not the eternal attribute.
3
Examine the consensus proof
The first proof argues that all who affirm the real attribute of speech consider it eternal; thus saying it is temporal would be a third opinion breaking consensus.
4
Examine the impossibility proof
The second proof uses a disjunctive argument: if speech were temporal, it must either inhere in Allah (impossible) or not (impossible, because an attribute must be inherent).
This proof relies on the principle that an attribute cannot belong to something without inhering in it.
5
Reflect on the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that the Mu'tazila agree with Ash'aris on the existence of the same attribute; Razi clarifies they deny the very attribute Ash'aris affirm.

Source Text

فأما نحن قد بينا أن الذي يقول به المعتزلة فنحن نقول به من حيث المعنى والذي نقول به فهم لا يقولون به البتة،

نقيم الدلالة على قدمها فإنهم يخالفوننا في المواضع الثلاثة فنقول .

Issue: The speech of Allah Almighty is eternal, contrary to the Mu'tazila and the Karamiyya. Know that the majority of us believe that the Mu'tazila agree with us that He Almighty is speaking, but disagree with us about the eternality of speech. As for us, we have made clear that what the Mu'tazila affirm we affirm in meaning, and what we affirm they do not affirm at all. So when we attempt to debate the Mu'tazila, it is necessary for us to investigate the essence of speech, then establish the proof that Allah Almighty is described by it, then establish the proof of its eternality, for they disagree with us in these three positions. As for the first two positions, which are the difficult ones with the Mu'tazila, the discussion of them has preceded. As for the third, the proof for it is from two aspects. The first: that the speakers are two—one who acknowledges that Allah Almighty is described by this speech, and one who denies that. And everyone who acknowledges it says it is eternal, because the Mu'tazila and the Karamiyya did not acknowledge that Allah Almighty is described by this speech; rather they asserted the temporality of speech that is letter and sound. If that is established, then if we were to assert the temporality of this speech, that would be a third opinion, a breach of consensus, and it is false. The second: This speech, if it were temporal, then either it would occur in the essence of Allah Almighty, making Him a locus of temporal events—and that is impossible—or it would not occur in Him, also impossible, because Allah Almighty being speaking, we have proven that it is among His attributes, and it is impossible for a thing's attribute not to be inherent in it; otherwise it would be permissible for a body to be moving by a motion subsisting in another, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage opens a new issue (mas'ala) concerning the speech of Allah. Razi first clarifies his understanding of the Mu'tazila's position: they agree that Allah is 'speaking' (mutakallim) but deny that His speech is eternal. Razi argues that the Ash'ari and Mu'tazili meanings of 'speech' differ fundamentally. He then outlines a three-step method for debating them: (1) define the essence of speech, (2) prove that Allah is described by it, (3) prove its eternality—and notes that steps (1) and (2) were already covered. For step (3), he gives two proofs. The first proof is from consensus (ijma'): all who affirm that Allah is described by this (real, eternal) speech hold it to be eternal; the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya deny that Allah is described by this speech altogether, so to say it is temporal would be a third opinion, breaking consensus. The second proof is from the impossibility of accidents in Allah (al-muhal al-ihdath): if speech were temporal, it would have to either subsist in Allah's essence (making Him a locus of temporals, which is impossible) or subsist in another (which would make His attribute of speech not truly His). Razi emphasises that an attribute must inhere in the one described. Both proofs lead to the conclusion that divine speech is eternal.

Key Terms
كلام الله
قديم
معتزلة
كرامية
إجماع
محل للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila agree with Ash'aris on the existence of the same attribute of speech, differing only on its eternality.
Correction: Razi clarifies that the Mu'tazila deny the very attribute of speech that Ash'aris affirm; they only affirm a temporal speech of letters and sounds.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why is it a 'breach of consensus' to say divine speech is temporal?
A) Because all Muslims agree it is eternal.
B) Because everyone who affirms that Allah is described by real speech says it is eternal.
C) Because the Mu'tazila already said it is temporal.
D) Because the Quran is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is eternal; the Mu'tazila and Karamiyya deny the very attribute, not just its eternality, and two proofs (consensus and impossibility of accidents) confirm the Ash'ari position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly feel that you are engaging with Allah's eternal, uncreated speech? Or do you treat it as a human-like text? What would change in your heart if you lived with the certainty that every verse is directly from His eternal attribute?
?
Razi shows that the Mu'tazila's denial of the eternal attribute is not just a theological error but a fundamental misrecognition of Allah. Examine your own life: are there times when you deny the reality of Allah's attributes in practice—acting as if He does not see, hear, or speak to you? How can you realign your actions with the fact that His attributes are real and inherent?
?
The second proof argues that an attribute must truly inhere in the described; it cannot be external. Consider your own faith: are Allah's attributes merely intellectual concepts you affirm, or do they inhere in your heart, shaping your fear, hope, and love? What step can you take today to let the attribute of His eternal speech penetrate your soul?

The Futility Objection and the Command Without Commanded
Razi presents the first Mu'tazili objection and its detailed Ash'ari answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the Mu'tazili objection that an eternal command without an existing object is futile, and the two main Ash'ari responses to this objection.

Core Idea
An eternal command exists without a commanded person; the command applies upon existence.

The first objection against the eternality of divine speech is that a command without a commanded object is pointless (عبث). Razi presents the Ash'ari responses, including the view that the very same eternal command becomes applicable to persons when they come into existence. This lesson unpacks the logic behind these answers.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial answer
Read the first objection and Abdullah ibn Sa'eed's extreme view, which Razi dismisses as unknowable.
Notice how Razi distinguishes intelligible speech from the specific modalities of command/prohibition.
2
Examine the majority view
Focus on the two sub-answers: the non-existent as commanded on assumption of existence, and the command without commanded that later applies.
Consider the example of the father's will to understand how a command can precede the commanded.
3
Reflect on the lesson's key idea
Ask yourself: Can a timeless command truly apply to temporal beings? How does this defend divine speech?
This connects to the broader attribute of speech being eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجوا بأمور . أولها : أن الأمر بلا مأمور عبث وهو غير جائز على الله تعالى .
وثانيها : أنه تعالى في الأزل لو كان متكلما بقوله إنا أرسلنا نوحا، وهو إخبار عن الماضي لكان كاذبا
وثالثها : أن الأمة مجمعة على أن كلام الله ناسخ ومنسوخ وسور وآيات وذلك من صفات المحدثات .
•
والجواب عن الأول : أن عبد الله بن سعيد ذهب إلى أن كلام الله تعالى وإن كان قديما لكنه ما كان في الأزل أمرا ولا نهيا ولا خبرا ثم صار فيما لا يزال كذلك وهذا في غاية البعد، لأنا لما وجدنا في النفس طلميا [؟] واقتضاء وبينا الفرق بينه وبين الإرادة أمكننا بعد ذلك أن نشير إلى ماهية معقولة وندعي ثبوتها لله تعالى فأما الكلام الذي يغاير هذه الحروف والأصوات ويغاير ماهية الأمر والنهي والخبر فغير معلوم التصور فكان القول بثبوته لله تعالى في الأزل محض الجهالة
•
أما جمهور الأصحاب : فقد زعموا أن كلام الله تعالى كان أمرا ونهيا في الأزل، ثم منهم من يقول المعدوم مأمور على تقدير الوجود وهذا في غاية البعد، لأن الجماد إذا لم يجز أن يكون مأمورا فالمعدوم، والذي هو في محض العدم كيف يعقل أن يكون مأمورا ومنهم من قال إنه في الأزل كان أمرا من غير مأمور، ثم لما استمر وبقي صار المكلفون بعد دخولهم في الوجود مأمورين بذلك الأمر وضربوا له مثالا وهو أن الإنسان إذا أخبره النبي الصادق بأن الله تعالى سيرزقه ولدا ولكنه مات قبل ولادته فإنه ربما قال لبعض الناس إذا أدركت ولدي بالغا فقل له أباك يأمرك بتحصيل العلم فهنا قد وجد الأمر والمأمور معدوم، حتى أنه لو بقي ذلك الأمر إلى أوان بلوغ ذلك الصبي لصار مأمورا بذلك الأمر .
وعن
الثاني : أن الخبر في الأزل واحد ولكنه مختلف الإضافة بحسب اختلاف الأوقات وبحسب ذلك تختلف الألفاظ الدالة عليه كما في العلم .
وعن
الثالث : أن تلك الصفات عائدة إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات ولا نزاع فيه، إنما الكلام في الصفة القديمة التي دلت هذه العبارات عليها
They objected with several matters. First: that a command without an object commanded is futile, and that is not permissible for Allah Almighty. Second: that if in pre-eternity He were speaking His words 'We sent Noah' – which is an information about the past – He would be lying. Third: that the community is agreed that the speech of Allah is abrogating and abrogated, surahs and verses, and that is among the characteristics of temporal things. The answer to the first: that Abdullah ibn Sa'eed held that the speech of Allah Almighty, although eternal, was in pre-eternity not a command, nor a prohibition, nor information, then it became so in what will never cease, and this is extremely far-fetched. Because we found in the soul demand [?] and requirement, and we explained the difference between it and will, we can after that point to an intelligible essence and claim its establishment for Allah Almighty. But the speech that is different from these letters and sounds and different from the essence of command, prohibition, and information is not known in conception; thus the assertion of its existence for Allah Almighty in pre-eternity is pure ignorance. As for the majority of companions: they claimed that the speech of Allah Almighty was command and prohibition in pre-eternity. Then some of them say: the non-existent is commanded on the assumption of existence, and this is extremely far-fetched, because if a lifeless object cannot be commanded, then the non-existent, and that which is in pure non-existence, how can it be conceived to be commanded? And some of them said: in pre-eternity it was a command without a commanded, then when it persisted and remained, the obligated persons, after their entry into existence, became commanded by that command. They gave an example for it: a person informed by a truthful prophet that Allah will grant him a son, but he dies before his birth; he might say to some people: 'If you encounter my son as an adult, say to him: your father commands you to acquire knowledge.' Here the command and the commanded are both non-existent, such that if that command remained until the time of that boy's maturity, he would become commanded by that command. As for the second: that the information in pre-eternity is one, but its relation differs according to the differences of times, and according to that the expressions indicating it differ, as in the case of knowledge. As for the third: that those characteristics belong to these letters and sounds, and there is no dispute about that; the discussion is only about the eternal attribute which these expressions indicate.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents three objections raised by opponents against the eternality of divine speech, followed by Razi's responses. The first objection: a command without an existing commanded object is vain (عبث), and Allah does not do vain things. Razi's answer: he first mentions Ibn Sa'eed's extreme view that eternal speech was not originally command/prohibition/information but became so afterwards, which Razi rejects as unknowable. He then presents the view of the majority of Ash'ari companions: the speech was already command and prohibition in pre-eternity. To the objection that there was no commanded person, they give two sub-answers: (a) the non-existent can be considered commanded on the assumption of existence, though this is problematic because even lifeless things cannot be commanded; (b) the command existed without a commanded object, and when persons come into existence they become commanded by that same eternal command. They illustrate with a hypothetical will: a father commands his unborn son, and the command exists even before the son's birth. The second objection: if Allah's speech 'We sent Noah' is eternal, then in pre-eternity it would be about a past event that hadn't happened, making it false. Razi's answer: the eternal information (خبر) is one, but its relation (إضافة) varies with time; the same applies to divine knowledge. The third objection: the Quran has abrogating and abrogated verses, implying change, which is a property of temporal things. Razi's answer: those characteristics apply to the letters and sounds of revelation, not to the eternal attribute itself; no one disputes that the recited Quran is temporal.

Key Terms
أمر بلا مأمور
عبث
مأمور
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That an eternal command cannot exist without an existing commanded object, making it futile.
Correction: The Ash'ari response shows that the command can be eternal and apply to future existents, similar to a will.

Checkpoint
According to one Ash'ari response, how does an eternal command apply to temporally existing persons?
A) The command is created anew each time.
B) The command existed without a commanded, and the commanded becomes commanded upon existence.
C) The command only applies to angels.
D) The command is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
An eternal divine command is not futile because it applies to persons when they come into existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a command in the Quran, do you feel it is a timeless message for you today, or do you dismiss it as only for the original audience? Will you pause and ask Allah to show you how to obey that command in your current circumstances?
?
If you truly believed that every divine command is eternally addressed to you as an individual, what would you change in your daily life? Which command have you been delaying to fulfill?
?
The father's will analogy shows that a command can exist before the child is born. Do you ever feel that Allah's commands are irrelevant because they were given long ago? How can you train yourself to see each command as a personal letter from Allah to you, written before you were even born?

The Temporal Information Objection and the Unity of Eternal News
Razi answers the objection about eternal information about the past using relative aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi answers the objection that an eternal information about the past would be false before the event, using the concept of relative aspects (إضافة).

Core Idea
Eternal information (khabar) is one but its relation varies with time, preventing falsehood.

The second Mu'tazili objection is that if Allah's speech 'We sent Noah' is eternal, then in pre-eternity it would be an information about a past event that hadn't occurred, making it false. Razi's concise answer appeals to the unity of the eternal attribute and its multiple relations. This lesson explains that key concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the second objection and Razi's answer. Note how he compares it to divine knowledge.
The answer is very brief: the eternal information is one but its relation differs with times.
2
Understand the concept of idafa
Idafa (إضافة) means relation or aspect. The same eternal speech relates to different times without change in itself.
Just as divine knowledge of past and future events does not change, the eternal news does not change either.
3
Apply to the example
Consider the statement 'We sent Noah'. In pre-eternity, it relates to a future event; after the event, it relates to a past event. The eternal speech is unchanged.
This preserves the truthfulness of the eternal speech.

?

?
Before an event happens, Allah's eternal speech describes it as if it already occurred. Does this give you confidence that He has already decreed and written your future? What fear or anxiety can you release now because you know His word about your life is already settled in eternity?
?
The objection raised here is that an eternal statement about a past event would be false before the event. How often do you judge God's actions or words based on your limited time-frame? Will you commit to viewing His eternal speech as always true, even when your current moment seems to contradict it?

The Abrogation Objection and the Distinction Between Eternal and Temporal Aspects
Razi replies to the abrogation objection by separating eternal attribute from temporal expressions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi answers the objection that abrogation (naskh) and variation in the Quran imply temporality, by distinguishing between the eternal attribute and the temporal expressions.

Core Idea
Abrogation and variation apply to the letters and sounds, not to the eternal attribute of speech.

The third objection is based on the observed phenomena of abrogation (ناسخ ومنسوخ) and varying surahs and verses in the Quran, which are characteristics of temporal things. Razi's answer is clear: these characteristics belong to the revealed expressions, not to the eternal attribute of speech itself. This lesson sharpens that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the third objection and Razi's answer. Notice that he concedes the temporal nature of the recited Quran.
The key is where the change occurs: in the created words, not in the eternal attribute.
2
Distinguish between eternal attribute and temporal expressions
Razi says 'those characteristics belong to these letters and sounds' – the eternal attribute is free from change.
This is a standard Ash'ari position: the eternal speech (kalam nafsi) is one, while the revealed Quran (kalam lafzi) is created.
3
Understand the implication
The objection is only effective if one confuses the two levels. Razi shows the confusion.
This defends divine speech from being temporal while accepting the Quran's createdness as recited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجوا بأمور . أولها : أن الأمر بلا مأمور عبث وهو غير جائز على الله تعالى .

وثالثها : أن الأمة مجمعة على أن كلام الله ناسخ ومنسوخ وسور وآيات وذلك من صفات المحدثات .
•
والجواب عن الأول : أن عبد الله بن سعيد ذهب إلى أن كلام الله تعالى وإن كان قديما لكنه ما كان في الأزل أمرا ولا نهيا ولا خبرا ثم صار فيما لا يزال كذلك وهذا في غاية البعد، لأنا لما وجدنا في النفس طلميا [؟] واقتضاء وبينا الفرق بينه وبين الإرادة أمكننا بعد ذلك أن نشير إلى ماهية معقولة وندعي ثبوتها لله تعالى فأما الكلام الذي يغاير هذه الحروف والأصوات ويغاير ماهية الأمر والنهي والخبر فغير معلوم التصور فكان القول بثبوته لله تعالى في الأزل محض الجهالة
•
أما جمهور الأصحاب : فقد زعموا أن كلام الله تعالى كان أمرا ونهيا في الأزل، ثم منهم من يقول المعدوم مأمور على تقدير الوجود وهذا في غاية البعد، لأن الجماد إذا لم يجز أن يكون مأمورا فالمعدوم، والذي هو في محض العدم كيف يعقل أن يكون مأمورا ومنهم من قال إنه في الأزل كان أمرا من غير مأمور، ثم لما استمر وبقي صار المكلفون بعد دخولهم في الوجود مأمورين بذلك الأمر وضربوا له مثالا وهو أن الإنسان إذا أخبره النبي الصادق بأن الله تعالى سيرزقه ولدا ولكنه مات قبل ولادته فإنه ربما قال لبعض الناس إذا أدركت ولدي بالغا فقل له أباك يأمرك بتحصيل العلم فهنا قد وجد الأمر والمأمور معدوم، حتى أنه لو بقي ذلك الأمر إلى أوان بلوغ ذلك الصبي لصار مأمورا بذلك الأمر .
وعن
الثاني : أن الخبر في الأزل واحد ولكنه مختلف الإضافة بحسب اختلاف الأوقات وبحسب ذلك تختلف الألفاظ الدالة عليه كما في العلم .
وعن
الثالث : أن تلك الصفات عائدة إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات ولا نزاع فيه، إنما الكلام في الصفة القديمة التي دلت هذه العبارات عليها
They objected with several matters. First: that a command without an object commanded is futile, and that is not permissible for Allah Almighty. Second: that if in pre-eternity He were speaking His words 'We sent Noah' – which is an information about the past – He would be lying. Third: that the community is agreed that the speech of Allah is abrogating and abrogated, surahs and verses, and that is among the characteristics of temporal things. The answer to the first: that Abdullah ibn Sa'eed held that the speech of Allah Almighty, although eternal, was in pre-eternity not a command, nor a prohibition, nor information, then it became so in what will never cease, and this is extremely far-fetched. Because we found in the soul demand [?] and requirement, and we explained the difference between it and will, we can after that point to an intelligible essence and claim its establishment for Allah Almighty. But the speech that is different from these letters and sounds and different from the essence of command, prohibition, and information is not known in conception; thus the assertion of its existence for Allah Almighty in pre-eternity is pure ignorance. As for the majority of companions: they claimed that the speech of Allah Almighty was command and prohibition in pre-eternity. Then some of them say: the non-existent is commanded on the assumption of existence, and this is extremely far-fetched, because if a lifeless object cannot be commanded, then the non-existent, and that which is in pure non-existence, how can it be conceived to be commanded? And some of them said: in pre-eternity it was a command without a commanded, then when it persisted and remained, the obligated persons, after their entry into existence, became commanded by that command. They gave an example for it: a person informed by a truthful prophet that Allah will grant him a son, but he dies before his birth; he might say to some people: 'If you encounter my son as an adult, say to him: your father commands you to acquire knowledge.' Here the command and the commanded are both non-existent, such that if that command remained until the time of that boy's maturity, he would become commanded by that command. As for the second: that the information in pre-eternity is one, but its relation differs according to the differences of times, and according to that the expressions indicating it differ, as in the case of knowledge. As for the third: that those characteristics belong to these letters and sounds, and there is no dispute about that; the discussion is only about the eternal attribute which these expressions indicate.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents three objections raised by opponents against the eternality of divine speech, followed by Razi's responses. The first objection: a command without an existing commanded object is vain (عبث), and Allah does not do vain things. Razi's answer: he first mentions Ibn Sa'eed's extreme view that eternal speech was not originally command/prohibition/information but became so afterwards, which Razi rejects as unknowable. He then presents the view of the majority of Ash'ari companions: the speech was already command and prohibition in pre-eternity. To the objection that there was no commanded person, they give two sub-answers: (a) the non-existent can be considered commanded on the assumption of existence, though this is problematic because even lifeless things cannot be commanded; (b) the command existed without a commanded object, and when persons come into existence they become commanded by that same eternal command. They illustrate with a hypothetical will: a father commands his unborn son, and the command exists even before the son's birth. The second objection: if Allah's speech 'We sent Noah' is eternal, then in pre-eternity it would be about a past event that hadn't happened, making it false. Razi's answer: the eternal information (خبر) is one, but its relation (إضافة) varies with time; the same applies to divine knowledge. The third objection: the Quran has abrogating and abrogated verses, implying change, which is a property of temporal things. Razi's answer: those characteristics apply to the letters and sounds of revelation, not to the eternal attribute itself; no one disputes that the recited Quran is temporal.

Key Terms
ناسخ ومنسوخ
سور وآيات
الصفة القديمة
الحروف والأصوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That abrogation and variation in the Quran prove that divine speech itself is temporal and changeable.
Correction: These phenomena apply only to the temporal expressions (kalam lafzi), not to the eternal attribute (kalam nafsi).

Checkpoint
According to Razi, where do the characteristics of abrogation and division into surahs belong?
A) To the eternal attribute of speech.
B) To the letters and sounds (the recited Quran).
C) To both equally.
D) To the minds of the interpreters.

Key Takeaway
The eternal attribute of divine speech is not subject to change; abrogation only affects the temporal expressions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite a verse that abrogates a previous command, do you ever doubt God's consistency? How does separating the eternal attribute from the temporal expressions help you trust His unchanging wisdom?
?
If the eternal attribute of speech is indivisible and unchanging, does your attention while reciting reflect the weight of that eternal reality, or do you treat the words as ordinary? What would change if you truly believed you are connecting to God's eternal attribute?
?
The abrogation in the Quran shows God's responsiveness to human situations. Does this encourage you to see His commands as living guidance rather than static rules? How will you adjust your attitude toward seemingly contradictory verses?

The Eternal Attribute and Temporal Signs of Speech
Refutation of Ibn Sa'eed's view that eternal speech can change, with a clarification of the correct view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the editorial commentator's distinction between the eternal attribute of speech and the temporal sounds and letters that indicate it.

Core Idea
The speech of Allah is eternal, but its revealed form changes without altering the attribute.

The commentator directly challenges Ibn Sa'eed's assertion that eternal speech can change. He argues that change implies temporality, and instead proposes a careful distinction: the attribute of speech is immutable, while the sounds and letters that convey it are temporal and subject to change, multiplicity, and descent. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, paying attention to the commentator's rejection of Ibn Sa'eed's view.
Notice the phrase 'باطل بوجه آخر' which indicates another refutation.
2
Identify the key distinction
Find where the commentator distinguishes between the eternal attribute and the temporal signs. Note the terms used: صفة قديمة for the attribute, and حروف وأصوات for the signs.
The commentator says 'يمكن كون الأصوات والحروف...' which is the core of the distinction.
3
Reflect on the argument
Ask yourself: Why does the commentator say change implies transition or occurrence? How does this distinction answer Ibn Sa'eed?
Change requires something temporal; the attribute is eternal, so it cannot change. But the sounds and letters are temporal, so they can change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) أقول قول عبد الله بن سعيد أن الكلام الأزلي قد يتغير باطل بوجه آخر وهو أن التغير لا يمكن إلا عند انتقال أو حدوث شيء لا يمكن أن يتغير، والأولى أن يقال الكلام وإن كان صفة قديمة يمكن كون الأصوات والحروف الدالة على تلك الصفة مما نزل على الأنبياء وسمعوها وبلغوها إلى أممهم فهي الموصوفة بالتغير والتكثير والنزول لا مدلولها التي هي تلك الصفة القديمة
·
وقوله : هذا الكلام لو كان محدثا لكان إما أن يحدث في ذات الله تعالى وهو ممنوع .
أقول : هذا هو مذهب الكرامية وهم يجوزون أن يكون الله تعالى محلا للحوادث .
وقوله : أو لا يحدث وهو محال لان كونه تعالى متكلما من صفاته وصفة الشيء تستحيل أن لا تكون حاصلة فيه. أقول : المتكلم صفة والكلام يجوز أن يكون في غيره كما أن الخالق والرازق صفة والخلق والرزق لا يجب أن يكون موجودا فيه، وباقي الكلام ظاهر .
(1) I say: The statement of Abdullah ibn Sa'eed that the eternal speech can change is false from another aspect: that change is only possible when there is transition or occurrence of something that can change. It is better to say: speech, even if it is an eternal attribute, it is possible for the sounds and letters indicating that attribute to be among what was revealed to the prophets, and they heard them and conveyed them to their communities. So these sounds and letters are described with change, multiplicity, and descent, not what they indicate which is that eternal attribute. And his statement: 'This speech, if it were temporal, would either occur in the essence of Allah—and that is impossible' —I say: This is the doctrine of the Karamiyya, and they permit that Allah Almighty be a locus of temporal events. And his statement: 'Or it would not occur in Him, also impossible, because Allah being speaking is among His attributes, and it is impossible for an attribute of a thing not to be inherent in it.' I say: The description 'speaking' is an attribute (sifa), and speech may be in another, just as 'Creator' and 'Provider' are attributes, but creation and provision are not required to be present in Him. The rest of the speech is clear.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This is an editorial note commenting on the previous discussion. The commentator rejects Abdullah ibn Sa'eed's idea that eternal speech can change, arguing that change implies something temporal. Instead, the correct view is that while the eternal attribute of speech is unchanging, the revealed sounds and letters that indicate it are temporal and subject to change, multiplicity, and descent. The commentator then responds to two points from Razi's second proof. First, Razi's claim that it is impossible for speech to occur in Allah's essence—the commentator notes that the Karamiyya actually consider this permissible. Second, Razi's argument that if speech did not occur in Allah, it would not be His attribute—the commentator disagrees, using the analogy of God being 'Creator' and 'Provider': these attributes are true of God even though creation and provision are not inhering in Him. Thus the speech could be in another entity (like the Preserved Tablet) while still being God's attribute.

Key Terms
تغير
صفة قديمة
حروف
أصوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal speech can change
Correction: The eternal attribute of speech is immutable; only the temporal sounds and letters that indicate it change.

Checkpoint
According to the editorial note, what undergoes change, multiplicity, and descent?
A) The eternal attribute of speech
B) The sounds and letters indicating the attribute
C) Both the attribute and the sounds
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The eternal attribute of God's speech is unchanging; only the temporal signs that convey it are subject to change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you treat the words as merely temporal sounds, or do you recognize that they point to an eternal attribute? How does this awareness change the way you approach every verse?
?
If the eternal speech of Allah is unchanging, yet the words you read change with your voice and pronunciation, where is your reverence directed — at the sounds or at the One who speaks eternally? Examine your heart: do you sometimes become more focused on the beauty of your recitation than on the eternal meaning behind it?
?
The passage teaches that change belongs only to temporal signs. In your daily life, do you find yourself treating Allah's commands as subject to change when they inconvenience you? How can you submit to the unwavering eternal speech even when your circumstances change?

Speech as an Attribute Without Inherence
Response to Razi's proof on inherence of speech, citing Karamiyya and using analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the commentator's response to Razi's argument that speech must inhere in Allah, using the analogy of Creator and Provider.

Core Idea
An attribute can belong to God without inherence, just as creation is God's attribute but not in His essence.

In this part of the editorial note, the commentator addresses two points from Razi's proof for the eternity of speech. First, he notes that the Karamiyya sect actually allows temporal events to occur in Allah's essence. Second, he contests Razi's claim that if speech does not inhere in Allah, it cannot be His attribute. Using a powerful analogy—that God is called 'Creator' and 'Provider' even though creation and provision are not in His essence—he shows that speech can be God's attribute while existing elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the commentator's two responses: one regarding the Karamiyya and one regarding the analogy.
The passage begins with 'وقوله : هذا الكلام لو كان محدثا'.
2
Understand the Karamiyya position
The commentator mentions that the Karamiyya allow Allah to be a locus of temporal events. Why is this relevant to Razi's argument?
Razi assumed it is impossible for speech to occur in Allah's essence, but the Karamiyya disagree.
3
Analyze the analogy
The commentator compares 'speaking' to 'Creator' and 'Provider'. How does this analogy show that an attribute can be true of God without inherence?
Just as God is called Creator even though the act of creation is not in His essence, so He is called Speaking even if speech is not in His essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the commentator, which analogy weakens Razi's claim that speech must inhere in Allah?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe Allah is al-Khaliq (the Creator), yet creation is not in His essence. You believe He is ar-Raziq (the Provider), yet provision is not in His essence. Now you learn that He is al-Mutakallim (the Speaker), yet speech need not be in His essence. Are you ready to submit to these truths even when your mind struggles to comprehend how an attribute can be real without inherence? Pray for tawfiq to accept revelation over reasoning.
?
The Karamiyya allowed that Allah can be a locus of temporal events. Does this idea disturb you? Examine why: is it because you have an implicit assumption that Allah must be absolutely unchanging? Is that assumption from the Quran or from your own philosophy? Will you search the Quran to see if it supports your view or challenges it?
?
When you recite the Quran, you believe you are uttering Allah's speech. But if that speech does not inhere in Allah, where is it? It exists on the Preserved Tablet, on your tongue, in your heart—yet remains His attribute. Does this make you feel closer to the Quran or more distant? Commit to reciting one verse today with the full awareness that you are carrying His speech, even if not contained in Him.

The Unity of the Eternal Attribute of Speech
Razi argues for the unity of the eternal attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that the eternal attribute of speech is one and not multiple, and how he reduces various forms of speech to information.

Core Idea
The eternal attribute of speech is essentially one: all forms reduce to information.

This passage addresses a key debate within the Ash'ari school: is the eternal attribute of speech (kalam) one or multiple? Some scholars posited five distinct 'words' (command, prohibition, etc.). Razi counters that they are all fundamentally informational, thus the attribute remains single. Understanding this argument helps clarify the unity of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal translation. Note the opponents' fivefold division and Razi's counterposition.
The passage is short but dense; take time to absorb the terms.
2
Identify the five types and Razi's reduction
List the five types mentioned (command, prohibition, information, inquiry, call). Then locate Razi's reasoning: command and prohibition are actually forms of information because they inform about reward and punishment.
Consider how this reduction works logically.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Think about why preserving the oneness of the attribute matters for tawhid. How does this argument prevent multiplicity in the divine essence?
This connects to broader discussions about divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : هذه الصفة القديمة المسماة بالكلام عندنا واحدة خلافا لبعض أصحابنا) فإنهم أثبتوا خمس كلمات الأمر والنهى والخبر والاستخبار والنداء. لما حقيقة الكلام هي الخبر والأمر والنهي أيضا خبر، لأنه إخبار عن ترتب الثواب والعقاب على الفعل والترك
Issue: This eternal attribute called 'speech' is, according to us, one, contrary to some of our companions. For they affirmed five 'words': command, prohibition, information, inquiry, and call. Because the reality of speech is information (khabar); command and prohibition are also information, because they are information about the arrangement of reward and punishment upon action and omission.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This is a short but significant issue: the unity of the eternal attribute of speech. Razi affirms that the one eternal attribute called 'speech' (kalam) is unitary, rejecting the view of some Ash'ari scholars who held that there are five distinct 'words': command (amr), prohibition (nahy), information (khabar), inquiry (istikhbar), and call (nida'). Razi's argument is that the true essence of speech is information (khabar); command and prohibition are actually types of information, because they inform about the consequences (reward and punishment) of actions. Therefore, the multiplicity is only in the expressions, not in the eternal attribute itself.

Key Terms
صفة واحدة
الكلام
الأمر
النهي
الخبر
الاستخبار
النداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the different types of speech (command, prohibition, etc.) imply multiple eternal attributes.
Correction: Razi argues that these types are all reducible to information, so the attribute remains one.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi consider command and prohibition to be forms of information?
A) Because they are temporary.
B) Because they inform about reward and punishment.
C) Because they are not part of the Quran.
D) Because the attribute of speech is created.

Key Takeaway
Razi preserves the unity of the divine attribute of speech by showing that its diverse expressions are all instances of information.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear a command in the Qur'an, do you primarily feel a sense of obligation, or do you hear it as information about the truth of reality and its consequences? Which response aligns more with Razi's argument?
?
Razi says that even prohibitions are information about punishment. If you internalized that every 'do not' is a truthful piece of information from the One who knows the harm, would your reluctance to sin be more about avoiding harm or about trusting His information? How can you train your heart to hear prohibitions as informative rather than restrictive?

The Truth of Allah's Information
Razi proves that Allah's information is true, not false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's two arguments that Allah's information is necessarily true and why an objection about the Arabic expressions does not undermine this.

Core Idea
Allah's information is true because lying is a deficiency and cannot be eternal.

In this short but dense issue, Razi establishes a foundational attribute of Allah: His speech (information) is necessarily true. He provides two concise arguments, one from perfection and one from the impossibility of eternal falsehood, then anticipates an objection about the specific Arabic expressions of the Quran. Despite the cut-off text, the core reasoning is complete and powerful.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim and first argument
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation up to 'محال' after the first argument. Notice that Razi begins by stating the issue (مسألة) and then gives the reason 'because lying is a deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for Allah.'
This argument relies on the attribute of perfection: Allah cannot have any deficiency.
2
Examine the second argument and its support
Read the second part: 'ولأنه لو كان كاذبا... وذلك معلوم بالضرورة.' This is a conditional argument: if Allah were a liar, the falsehood would be eternal, which would make truth impossible — an absurd consequence. Razi then supports it with a general principle about any knower being able to give truthful information.
The second argument uses the impossibility of opposites coexisting eternally.
3
Analyze the objection and Razi's reply
Read from 'لا يقال' to the end. The objector says: even if the eternal information is true, the specific Arabic words (الألفاظ) could be false. Razi's reply, though cut off, turns the objection against the Mu'tazila: they themselves allow omission and implication for hidden wisdom, so they cannot demand strict literal truth in every expression.
Razi shifts the burden: the Mu'tazila's own principles undermine their objection.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider what this passage teaches about divine attributes. Truth (صدق) is an essential attribute of Allah's speech, not dependent on the external form of revelation. The eternal attribute is what matters for truth, not the temporal expressions.
This defends the Ash'ari position that the Quran (as eternal speech) is true, while the recited words are created expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: خبر الله تعالى صدق .
لأن الكذب نقص وهو على الله محال، ولأنه لو كان كاذبا لكان كاذبا بكذب قديم ولو كان كذلك لاستحال منه الصدق والتالي محال، فإن كل من علم شيئا صح منه أن يخبر عن نفسه عنه خبرا صدقا وذلك معلوم بالضرورة .
لا يقال : هب أن ما ذكرته يدل على أن ذلك الخبر القديم صدق لكنه لا يدل على كون هذه الألفاظ صدقا. لانا نقول للمعتزلة : هذا أيضا لازم عليكم لأنكم جوزتم الحذف والإضمار للحكمة لا نطلع عليها وتجويز
Issue: The information of Allah Almighty is true. Because lying is a deficiency, and it is impossible for Allah. And because if He were a liar, He would be a liar by an eternal lie, and if that were the case, truth would be impossible from Him, and the consequent is impossible. Indeed, anyone who knows something, it is valid for him to inform about himself about it as a truthful report, and this is known necessarily. It cannot be said: Suppose what you have mentioned proves that the eternal information is true, but it does not prove that these expressions are true. For we say to the Mu'tazila: This also follows necessarily for you, because you have permitted omission and implication for a wisdom that we do not know, and permissibility.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This brief issue (mas'ala) establishes that Allah's information (khabar) is true (sidq). Razi gives two arguments: first, lying is a deficiency (naqs) and deficiency is impossible for Allah. Second, if Allah were a liar, His lie would be eternal, making truth impossible for Him—which is absurd. He then refutes an objection: even if the eternal information is true, what about the recited Arabic expressions? Razi replies by turning the objection against the Mu'tazila: they themselves allow omission and implication in the Quran for hidden wisdom, so they cannot demand strict literal truth in every expression. The argument appears incomplete due to the cut-off text, but the main point is clear: the eternal attribute of information is true, and objections about temporal expressions are not fatal.

Key Terms
خبر
صدق
كذب
نقص
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the truth of Allah's information depends on the literal truth of every Arabic expression in the Quran.
Correction: Razi distinguishes between the eternal attribute of information (which is true) and the temporal expressions. The expressions can involve omission and implication for divine wisdom without affecting the truth of the eternal speech.

Checkpoint
What is Razi's second argument for the truth of Allah's information?
A) Allah cannot lie because He is perfect.
B) If Allah were a liar eternally, truth would be impossible for Him.
C) The Quran says so.
D) All prophets agree.

Key Takeaway
Allah's information is true because falsehood would entail deficiency or impossibility of truth; an objection about specific words is addressed by noting that divine wisdom may involve omission and implication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The source says lying is a deficiency impossible for Allah. Reflect: where in your life do you excuse small lies? How does that contradict the attribute of truth you affirm for Allah? What will you change today?
?
Razi argues that someone who knows can truthfully inform. Why then do you act as if you don't know the truth of the Quran when you disobey? Write one specific area where you will align your actions with Allah's truthful information.

God's Report is Truthful by Necessity
Razi proves that God's report is truthful, refuting an objection from the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's rational argument that God's report must be truthful and his refutation of the Mu'tazilite objection regarding the literal words.

Core Idea
God's truthfulness is proven by necessity; lying is a deficiency impossible for God.

Razi presents a concise but powerful proof that God's speech must be truthful. He then anticipates an objection from the Mu'tazila who might separate the eternal speech from its verbal expression. This lesson walks through both the proof and the counter-argument, showing how Razi turns the objection back on his opponents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the translation, to grasp Razi's argument flow.
2
Identify the two main arguments
Notice the two reasons given: (1) lying is a deficiency impossible for God; (2) if God lied, His lie would be eternal, precluding truth. Underline these.
3
Examine the objection and refutation
Read the objection about the difference between eternal report and uttered words, and see how Razi retorts that the Mu'tazila's own position undermines certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: خبر الله تعالى صدق . لان الكذب نقص وهو على الله محال ، ولأنه لو كان كاذبا لكان كاذبا بكذب قديم ولو كان كذلك لاستحال منه الصدق والسكن التالى محال ، فإن كل من علم شيئا صح منه أن الخبر فى نفسه عنه خبرا صدقا وذلك معلوم بالضرورة . لا يقال : هب أن ماذكرته يدل على أن ذلك الخبر القديم صدق لكنه لا يدل على كون هذه الألفاظ صدقا. لانا نقول للمتزلة : هذا أيضاً لازم عليكم لانكم جوزتم الحذف والإضمار الحكمة لا نطلع عليها وتجويز ذلك يرفع الوثوق عن هذه الظواهر
Issue: God's report is truthful. Because lying is a deficiency and it is impossible for God, and because if He were a liar, He would be a liar with an eternal lie, and if that were the case, truth would be impossible from Him, and the second [possibility] is impossible. For everyone who knows something, it is valid that he gives a report about it that is truthful in itself, and that is known by necessity. It cannot be said: 'Suppose what you mentioned indicates that the eternal report is truthful, but it does not indicate that these words are truthful.' For we say to the Mu'tazila: This also follows upon you, because you allow omission and concealment for a wisdom we are not aware of, and allowing that removes certainty from these apparent expressions.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a proof and defense of the truthfulness of God's speech. The author gives two arguments: first, lying is a deficiency, which is impossible for God; second, if God were a liar, His lie would be eternal, and then truth would be impossible for Him, which is absurd. He then addresses an objection: the argument only proves the eternal report is truthful, not the actual words. The author retorts that the Mu'tazila themselves allow omission and concealment for unknown reasons, which undermines certainty in all revealed expressions.

Key Takeaway

Is the Eternal Speech Hearable?
Al-Razi questions the audibility of eternal speech via analogy with vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi doubts the audibility of the eternal speech and how he compares it to the case of vision.

Core Idea
Hearing and vision may have different criteria for their objects.

Al-Razi begins by stating that we know the eternal speech is heard by necessity. However, he then questions whether it is valid to say it is an object of hearing in the same way physical sounds are. He uses an analogy with vision to highlight a potential difference: while existence is the common cause for visibility, soundness might be the specific cause for audibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the key terms: مسموع (hearable), الرؤية (vision), العلة المشتركة (common cause).
2
Identify the two claims
Al-Razi first affirms necessary knowledge that the speech is heard, then expresses doubt about its being an object of hearing. Locate these two statements.
This sets up the problem.
3
Understand the analogy with vision
Al-Razi explains why we allowed vision of non-physical things: because existence is the common cause of visibility. He then contrasts this with hearing, where the common cause is not clear.
The analogy shows a potential logical gap.
4
Consider the implication for hearing
Since hearing relates to sounds, the cause for something being hearable may be its soundness. If the eternal speech is not a sound, it might not be hearable in that sense.
This is the core doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : نحن نعلم بالضرورة أن ذلك الكلام القديم مسموع الآن . وهل يصح أن يكون مسموعا، هذا ما لم يقم عندى عليه دليل ، لانا جوزنا رؤية ماليس بجسم ولا بعرض ، لأنه لما رأينا الجسم والعرض وثبت أنه لابد من علة مشتركة وأنه لا مشترك إلا الوجود لاجرم قلنا يجوز رؤية كل موجود ، وأما في هذه المسألة فالسمع لم يتعلق بالأجسام والأدوات حتى يفتقر إلى علة مشتركة ، بل السمع لم يتعلق بالأصوات فجاز أن تكون علة صحة المسموعية هي الصوتية فقط وحينئذ لا يكون ذلك الكلام مسموعا
Issue: We know by necessity that that eternal speech is heard now. But is it valid that it is heard? This is something for which no proof has come to me. Because we have allowed the vision of what is neither a body nor an accident, since we have seen body and accident and it was established that there must be a common cause, and there is no common [cause] except existence, therefore we said it is permissible to see every existent. But in this issue, hearing is not related to bodies and instruments so as to need a common cause; rather, hearing is not related to sounds, so it is possible that the cause of the validity of being heard is soundness only, and then that speech would not be heard.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a position on whether the eternal speech is audible. The author states that we know necessarily that it is heard, but whether it can be heard in the sense of being an object of hearing is another question. He admits he has no proof for that. He draws an analogy with vision: we allowed seeing non-corporeal things because existence is the common cause of visibility. However, for hearing, the common cause might be soundness, not existence, so the eternal speech might not be hearable.

Key Terms
مسموع
الرؤية
العلة المشتركة
الوجود
الصوتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The eternal speech is heard in the same physical way as sounds.
Correction: Al-Razi suggests that the cause of audibility might be soundness, so the eternal speech, being non-sound, may not be an object of hearing in that sense.

Checkpoint
Why does the author doubt that the eternal speech is heard?
A) Because hearing requires a body
B) Because the common cause for hearing might be soundness, not existence
C) Because the eternal speech is not a sound
D) Because he has no proof for vision

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi doubts that the eternal speech is hearable by the same criteria as sounds, because hearing may require soundness rather than existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the Quran, do you think you are hearing the eternal speech itself or a temporal sound that represents it? Honestly, does that distinction affect your reverence?
?
Al-Razi admits he has no proof that the eternal speech is hearable, despite knowing it as a matter of faith. Are there areas in your own belief where you rely on necessary knowledge without rational proof, and does that unsettle you or strengthen your trust?
?
If a great scholar like al-Razi can express uncertainty about a core theological issue, how comfortable are you with not having all the answers? What does that say about your humility before divine mysteries?

Refutation of Takwin as a Distinct Eternal Attribute
Razi refutes the Hanafi claim that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hanafi claim that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from power is rationally untenable according to Imam Razi.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot be both eternal and distinct from power without logical contradiction.

Imam Razi presents a concise logical refutation of the Hanafi doctrine of takwin (bringing into existence) as an eternal attribute. By examining the possible meanings of takwin, he shows that it either reduces to power or becomes temporal. This lesson walks through his argument and the key distinctions involved.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without parsing. Then read the translation to get the overall argument.
The text cuts off at the end, but the main argument is complete.
2
Identify the three possible meanings of takwin
Notice how Razi considers three interpretations: relative attribute, identical to power, or something else. See how each is handled.
3
Follow the objection and response
The opponents claim power affects validity while takwin affects actual existence. Razi counters by showing this leads to redundancy or impossibility.
Pay attention to the concept of 'validity' versus 'obligation'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : زعم بعض فقهاء الحنفية أن التكوين صفة أزلية الله تعالى وأن المسكون محدث . فنقول لهم : القول بأن التكوين قديم ومحدث يستدعى تصور ماهية التكوين ، فإن كان المراد منه نفس مؤثرية القدرة في المقدور فهى صفة نسبية والنسب لا يوجد إلا عند وجود المنتسبين فيلزم من حدوث المكون حدوث التكوين ، وإن عنيتم صفة مؤثرة في وجود الأثر فهى عين القدر وإن عنيتم به أمر اعمالنا فبينوه . قالوا : القدرة صفة مؤثرة في صحة وجود المقدورة والتكوين مؤثر فى نفس وجود المقدور . قلنا القدرة لا تأثير لها فى كون المقدور فى نفسه جائز الوجود . لأن ذلك له لذاته وما بالذات لا يكون بالغير فلم يبق إلا أن يكون تأثيرها في وجود المقدور تأثيرها على سبيل الصحة لا على سبيل الوجوب ، فلو أثبتنا صفة أخرى الله مؤثرة في وجود المقدور لمكان تأثيرها في المقدور ، وإن كان على سبيل الصحة كان عين القدرة فيلزم اجتماع المثلين ويلزم اجتماع صفتين مستقلتين بالتأثير على المقدور الواحد وهو محال ، وإن كان على سبيل
Issue: Some of the Hanafi jurists claimed that takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute of God and that the brought into existence is temporal. So we say to them: The statement that takwin is eternal and temporal requires conceiving the essence of takwin. If what is meant by it is the very effectiveness of power in the object of power, then it is a relative attribute, and relations exist only when the two relata exist, so the temporality of the brought-into-existence necessitates the temporality of takwin. If you mean an attribute effective in the existence of the effect, then it is identical to power. If you mean something else, then explain it. They said: Power is an attribute effective in the validity of existence of the object of power, while takwin is effective in the actual existence of the object of power. We reply: Power has no effect in the object of power being in itself possible of existence, because that belongs to itself, and what is by itself is not by another. So it remains that its effect in the existence of the object of power is on the way of validity, not on the way of obligation. If we posit another attribute effective in the existence of the object of power, if its effect is on the way of validity, then it is identical to power, leading to the coincidence of two similars, and the coincidence of two independent attributes affecting one object of power is impossible. And if it is on the way of ... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage refutes the Hanafi position that takwin (bringing into existence) is a distinct eternal attribute. The author analyzes the possible meanings: if it means the effectiveness of power, it is a relative attribute that would be temporal; if it means an effective attribute, it is identical to power. The opponents argue that power affects the validity of existence while takwin affects actual existence. The author counters that power's effect is on validity, and any other attribute with the same effect is redundant.

Key Terms
التكوين
القدرة
المقدور
الصفة النسبية
اجتماع المثلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Takwin is a separate eternal attribute distinct from power.
Correction: Razi argues that takwin is either identical to power or temporal; it cannot be an additional eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if takwin is a relative attribute (effectiveness of power), what follows?
A) It is eternal
B) It is temporal because relations require existent relata
C) It is identical to power
D) It is impossible

Key Takeaway
Takwin cannot be an eternal attribute distinct from power; it is either identical to power or temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate Allah's power, do you truly believe that nothing else is needed for Him to bring about existence, or do you unconsciously imagine a separate 'creative' force? How can you purify your understanding of tawhid from such hidden dualisms? Commit to one specific way you will correct this.
?
Razi demands clear conceptualization before debate. Do you hold yourself to the same standard when you speak about Allah's attributes, or do you often use terms without precise definitions? Pause and identify one area of your faith where you tend to be vague, and resolve to clarify it.
?
The principle 'what is by itself is not by another' is central to this argument. How does this truth change the way you view your own existence and your absolute reliance on Allah? Are you living as if your existence is self-sufficient? What practical step can you take today to acknowledge your complete dependence on Him?
